<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_34398573">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/34398573" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1586349-mb-what-she-read" class="left imgcol" title="MB (What she read)"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1224813098p2/1586349.jpg" alt="MB (What she read)" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/34398573?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 24, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1586349-mb-what-she-read" class="user" title="MB (What she read)">MB (What she read)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/64219.Maskerade" title="Paperback 9780061056918" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1586349-mb-what-she-read?shelf=contains-humor" class="actionLinkLite">contains-humor</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1586349-mb-what-she-read?shelf=fantasy-urban-fantasy-paranormals" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy-urban-fantasy-paranormals</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1586349-mb-what-she-read?shelf=re-read-in-2013" class="actionLinkLite">re-read-in-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer34398573">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16329559159849550630">Reread once again 10/24/13: I think the interactions between Granny and Nanny in this are some of my favorites for the witches. <br /><br />I confess, I always wish Pratchett would update us on Perdita/Agnes. I always feel sorry for her at the end of this book, and wish her future happiness...or at least, contentment with her lot. He seems to have switched over to Tiffany instead, and we <u>know</u> Tiffany is going to be <u>fine</u>. P/Agnes, not so much. I wish her (if that is what <u>she</u> wants) a fine young man who will</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16329559159849550630">Reread once again 10/24/13: I think the interactions between Granny and Nanny in this are some of my favorites for the witches. <br /><br />I confess, I always wish Pratchett would update us on Perdita/Agnes. I always feel sorry for her at the end of this book, and wish her future happiness...or at least, contentment with her lot. He seems to have switched over to Tiffany instead, and we <u>know</u> Tiffany is going to be <u>fine</u>. P/Agnes, not so much. I wish her (if that is what <u>she</u> wants) a fine young man who will appreciate her for the catch she is, and a successful and enjoyable career--in witching perhaps, but again, only if that is what <u>she</u> wants. <br /><br />I really feel unhappy that Agnes is left at the end of this book doomed to be the 'unwanted' maiden of the trio, faced with a future she dreads, no use for her amazing talent, and forced to wait hand and foot on Granny and Nanny. What a life! Agnes, you have my sympathy and I wish you luck!<br /><br />BTW, why does the sparkly brainless twit get the happy ending?!? This is completely unlike TP in other books.<br /><br />To me, this has one of the least satisfying conclusions of any of Pratchett's books.<br /><br />So: Here's my imaginary 'bonus material' for Agnes. She moves into Magrat's cottage, and transforms it into a beautiful nest. She offers music lessons to the youth of Lancre part-time, and develops her magic skills under Granny and Nanny's guidance, but still maintains her own strong sense of self worth. She does a bit of consciousness raising on the side. Once she has reached her pinnacle of attainment, and served out her apprenticeship, she packs up her valuables, turns over her cottage to the next 'maiden' in line, and takes off to first Ankh-Morpork, then the world. <br /><br />As Madame Perdita, she performs opera to crowned heads and opera afficianados across Discworld, loved by many, admired &amp; respected by all. Supported always by her faithful (and sexy) accompanist wherever she travels. She is always dressed in the finest of black haute couture set off by exquisite high-heeled black velvet or lace boots with her trademark red soles. <br /><br />At a fine old age, Agnes settles down in a villa in Genua with her accompanist, her world-famous chef, and her coterie of admirers. The hills are alive with the sound of music... And make sure you knock first, or at least cough loudly, before entering any grottos or nooks.<br /><br />A CHALLENGE FOR YOU: What is <em>YOUR</em> version of Agnes/Perdita's future? Feel free to post in the comments.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16329559159849550630">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer104592485">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10677114102138203376">There is no doubt that the Opera House of Ankh-Morpork is known for its off-beat musicals. An added attraction to these outrageous productions is the resident ghost. Ghostly activity seems go into overtime when the famous Enrico Basilica arrives on the scene. The ghost has the entire opera company terrorized. The only hope of getting things in order is to rid the theater of this pesky ghost. What better cover could witches Granny Weatherwax and Nanny Ogg hope for while they work to convince Agne</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10677114102138203376">There is no doubt that the Opera House of Ankh-Morpork is known for its off-beat musicals. An added attraction to these outrageous productions is the resident ghost. Ghostly activity seems go into overtime when the famous Enrico Basilica arrives on the scene. The ghost has the entire opera company terrorized. The only hope of getting things in order is to rid the theater of this pesky ghost. What better cover could witches Granny Weatherwax and Nanny Ogg hope for while they work to convince Agnes Nitt (aka Perdita X. Nitt) to join their coven. As everyone knows, you can't have a coven with less than three witches and Agnes has potential. Unfortunately for them, Agnes (who can sing harmony with herself) wants to be an opera singer. Murder and mayhem brings Death upon the scene and he is complaining that his scythe arm is sore from over use. There is no question that Granny and Nanny will solve the problem. While the solution is surprisingly logical, the process to the solution is laugh out loud funny.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_124083681">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/124083681" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4244557-alins" class="left imgcol" title="Alins"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1291743082p2/4244557.jpg" alt="Alins" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/124083681?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 25, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4244557-alins" class="user" title="Alins">Alins</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/78876.Maskerade" title="Hardcover 9780575058088" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer124083681">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6049626999766830649"><br />Nowadays I don't get all that many opportunities to open a new Terry Pratchett book. Countless years of reading him has left me patiently waiting for his next effort. So the discovery of one that I've missed is a moment to be treasured. So now, ten years after I should have read it, I've had the delight of reading Maskerade for the first time. Even better, it's a Lancre witches tale, starring the indomitable Granny Weatherwax, and Nanny Ogg, the original Benny Hill.<br /><br />"Wait," you exclaim, "Where's</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6049626999766830649"><br />Nowadays I don't get all that many opportunities to open a new Terry Pratchett book. Countless years of reading him has left me patiently waiting for his next effort. So the discovery of one that I've missed is a moment to be treasured. So now, ten years after I should have read it, I've had the delight of reading Maskerade for the first time. Even better, it's a Lancre witches tale, starring the indomitable Granny Weatherwax, and Nanny Ogg, the original Benny Hill.<br /><br />"Wait," you exclaim, "Where's Magrat?" Off to be queen, of course, leaving Nanny and Granny to party alone before the marshmallow toasting fire. Nanny decides the Agnes Nitt, a large girl with a very large voice would make the perfect replacement. Unfortunately Agnes has had another idea entirely. Tired of being the girl with the 'great personality' and 'beautiful hair' she has left Lancre for Ankh-Moorpark were she is trying to make her living as an opera extra.<br /><br />In Ankh-Moorpork, it should come as no surprise, the opera house comes complete with a whacko ghost with a white mask, a huge chandelier, and, of course, a beautiful blond named Christine. Agnes (now Perdita) can sing, but Christine cannot, so in no time we have a voice hoax, an angry ghost, and Nanny, Granny, and Greeb, the cat with the original bad attitude.<br /><br />Pratchett is merciless, as he lampoons witching, opera, publishing, cookbooks, show music, leaving home to make it in the big city, psychology, and growing up the hard way. Trust Esme Weatherwax and Nanny Ogg to find the loophole in everything the encounter, outmaneuver the villains, and bedazzle the crowds. Trust pratchett to leave no opportunity for wry humor unturned.<br /><br />Agnes/Perdita is a great character on her own. Too fat to be anything else but a 'nice' girl she also has a mind almost as sharp as Granny Weatherwax. Agnes doesn't want to be a witch because that is almost the only career opportunity Lancre has for someone with brains and generous proportions. But neither does she want to be a bump on a log. She has a knack for seizing those opportunities that appear, and enough sense to make it through her own identity crisis.<br /><br />While this isn't one of Pratchett's tour-de-farces, it is an excellent effort, one that you will relish for some time to come. The Lancre stories are consistently the most humane and personal of his efforts, while the Ankh-Moorpork tales tend to hand grander scopes and characterizations. Maskerade sits smack dab in the middle on an elephant all it's own. Have fun!<br />Help other customers find the most helpful reviews <br />Was this review helpful to you? Yes No<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6049626999766830649">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer16458933698073843945">There's a ghost in the Ankh-Morpork opera house. Murder mystery/opera/cook-book...Nanny and Granny Weatherwax save the day again. I finished up this book with a real affection for Granny Weatherwax. I liked her before, but I appreciated her after. Same goes for the witches as characters; I'll take Granny Weatherwax over the wizard Ridcully any day of the week. And I think that the unexpectedly real dilemma over Right and Wrong her character experienced through the story (how is Granny Weatherwax</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16458933698073843945">There's a ghost in the Ankh-Morpork opera house. Murder mystery/opera/cook-book...Nanny and Granny Weatherwax save the day again. I finished up this book with a real affection for Granny Weatherwax. I liked her before, but I appreciated her after. Same goes for the witches as characters; I'll take Granny Weatherwax over the wizard Ridcully any day of the week. And I think that the unexpectedly real dilemma over Right and Wrong her character experienced through the story (how is Granny Weatherwax any different from Black Aliss?) and how she finally choose to deal with Salzella is what won me over. There would have been easier, less painful ways to defeat him. But Granny Weatherwax recognized that overcoming evil without becoming evil must often come at a personal cost.<br /><br />A few minor walk-on scenes for Death, and a small but satisfying incorporation of the Librarian and Corporal Nobby Nobbs, who has to carry around an identification card to prove he's human. And quite a bit of scumble. Apples--or, mostly apples...<br /><br /></span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1174883554">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11579108577178419241">Another marvelous Discworld adventure with Nanny Ogg and Granny Weatherwax. This is a lively satire of opera and the use of disguises, and of music and musicians and theater and most of all the use of magic, which as usual turns out to be mostly "headology." I recognized all sorts of references to famous operas and musicals, and I suspect there were some that went over my head. If you're a Pratchett fan and you want to laugh out loud, this one's for you.</span>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/45141460" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1038815-jc" class="left imgcol" title="Jc"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1321228818p2/1038815.jpg" alt="Jc" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/45141460?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 02, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1038815-jc" class="user" title="Jc">Jc</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/64219.Maskerade" title="Paperback 9780061056918" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer45141460">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4164985882984899883">This was not one of the Pratchett Discworld books that was recommended to me by the two friends who were listing their favorites. I think I know why -- all the inside jokes are about the world of opera, not the favorite haunt of many people these days. However, being a fan of opera, I did really enjoy this D'World episode. And I don't think it is just for opera fans -- it also has the Witches, the favorite characters of one of my friends. The Witches are always fun to follow, and they are very c</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4164985882984899883">This was not one of the Pratchett Discworld books that was recommended to me by the two friends who were listing their favorites. I think I know why -- all the inside jokes are about the world of opera, not the favorite haunt of many people these days. However, being a fan of opera, I did really enjoy this D'World episode. And I don't think it is just for opera fans -- it also has the Witches, the favorite characters of one of my friends. The Witches are always fun to follow, and they are very central to this book. Also, for those of you who might like The Phantom of the Opera, that story is also a central part of Maskerade. And, if you just like Pratchett I think you will find this a pleasurable read.<br /><br />That makes 15 of these things I have read... amazing, I never thought I would be interested in reading any of them.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4164985882984899883">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vbMfW/w3x9G5GRfnMOMDNwUhKbhRYyUqxCgBVxDHdDnYZyCIDuXTKzXBY1xOguWFTNbqoRi+YoCuIQTF3FKCfA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {

    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett">About Terry Pratchett</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett"><img alt="1654" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1235562205p2/1654.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer6365638274983556053">Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <em>The Carpet People</em>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br /><br />Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, including his first Discworld novel,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6365638274983556053">Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <em>The Carpet People</em>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br /><br />Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, including his first Discworld novel, <em>The Color of Magic</em>, in 1983. In 1987, he turned to writing full time. <br /><br />There are over 40 books in the Discworld series, of which four are written for children. The first of these, <em>The Amazing Maurice and His Educated Rodents</em>, won the Carnegie Medal. <br /><br />A non-Discworld book, <em>Good Omens</em>, his 1990 collaboration with Neil Gaiman, has been a longtime bestseller and was reissued in hardcover by William Morrow in early 2006 (it is also available as a mass market paperback - Harper Torch, 2006 - and trade paperback - Harper Paperbacks, 2006). <br /><br />In 2008, Harper Children's published Terry's standalone non-Discworld YA novel, <em>Nation</em>. Terry published <em>Snuff</em> in October 2011. <br /><br />Regarded as one of the most significant contemporary English-language satirists, Pratchett has won numerous literary awards, was named an Officer of the British Empire “for services to literature” in 1998, and has received honorary doctorates from University of Warwick in 1999, the University of Portsmouth in 2001, the University of Bath in 2003, the University of Bristol in 2004, Buckinghamshire New University in 2008, the University of Dublin in 2008, Bradford University in 2009, University of Winchester in 2009, and The Open University in 2013 for his contribution to Public Service.<br /><br />In Dec. of 2007, Pratchett disclosed that he had been diagnosed with Alzheimer's disease. On 18 Feb, 2009, he was knighted by Queen Elizabeth II.<br /><br />He was awarded the World Fantasy Life Achievement Award in 2010.<br /><br />Sir Terry Pratchett passed away on 12th March 2015.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6365638274983556053">...more</a>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett" class="actionLink moreLink">More about Terry Pratchett...</a>
